<a id="t-6e5cad79b6"></a>
## Thread: My Win98 Upgrade experience — 2 msgs

### My Win98 Upgrade experience

- **From:** "Daniel Maltes" <dwm@frontiernet.net>
- **Date:** 1998-06-27T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<6n39be$2mce$1@node17.cwnet.frontiernet.net>`

```

I thought I'd share my Win98 Upgrade experience with my fellow COBOL
professionals.

To say the least, it was stressful and just plain did not go well.  But in
the end, successful.

Installation took about 45 minutes on a 200MMX PC with 64MB RAM, and at the
very end(you guessed it), the installation crashed.  Everything locked up
and died.  Aargh!!  "How could this be?", I thought.  Windows 95 ran fine
with all my drivers and peripherals and now the latest and greatest Windows
98 is crapping out!  I'm sure you could understand how hot under the collar
I was.

So, I hit the old reboot button on my PC and waited for the bad news to
appear on the screen.  Sure enough, "Windows protection error... Your system
must be rebooted."  Yikes!  What the heck did that mean.  No specifics, no
details, nada, nunca, zip, nothing!!  So, I rebooted again.  Same damn
message.

Well, by now it's midnight and I'm seeing red.  Do I go to bed and start in
the morning?  Heck no, I'm a stupid guy and I have to make this work.  I
paid $90 bucks for this ridiculous software, and it has to work!.

Next, I rebooted into safe mode.  It said some strange message about my
video settings and how it would have to use standard VGA mode.  "Fine.  Just
get on with it", I thought.  Finally, I get a desktop.  So where do I go
from here I thought.  I decided to check my c:\bootlog.txt file.  Nothing
revealing there.  So now what?

At this point, I figured it must be some older OEM peripheral driver that's
not compatible with Win98.  So I went into my control panel system settings
and removed a few things.  I removed my STB video driver, my joystick
driver, my 3Dfx video accelerator driver, and my gateway monitor driver.  I
figured I could reinstall newer drivers after I got Win98 up and running and
I was back on the internet.  I noticed I was getting sound in Win98, so I
left my sound card driver alone.

Then, I figured I better remove a few pieces of software that run when my
system starts.  They weren't in my start group, so I realized I'd better
remove them in the control panel add/remove programs option.  I got rid of
Norton Antivirus, and my Gravis Grip joystick software.

Well, time to reboot and cross my fingers.  Sure enough, Win98's
installation screen came up and the rest of the install continued.  The
install had crashed where it was trying to detect my hardware, so that's
where it picked up.  This time, it detected everything, and low and behold,
actually dialed the internet and downloaded the latest drivers for my video
card, 3Dfx accelerator, and plug and play monitor.  That sort of made up for
my aggravation, but not quite.

Anyway, I have a few tips to follow BEFORE running the upgrade:
1. Uninstall or turn off any software that runs when you boot-up Win95.
2. Remove your virus detection software.
3. Change your video settings to standard vga, and a standard monitor.
4. Remove drivers for video accelerators and joysticks.
5. Start early in the day so your not up all night!

Good luck! :)
```

```
you
can then go back to your previous OS with no problems (or at least with only
the
problems you had before attempting an upgrade).

DaveJ.
```

<a id="t-6d5a339829"></a>
## Thread: Priorities,objectives, mission statement for new cobol standard - my opinion — 1 msgs

_Topics: [`COBOL standards (ANS, ISO, 74/85/2002/2014)`](topics.md#standards)_

### Priorities,objectives, mission statement for new cobol standard - my opinion

- **From:** boonlee@melbpc.org.au (Boon Lee)
- **Date:** 1998-06-28T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<359617ab.8702102@news.melbpc.org.au>`

```

I have  used COBOL on ICL, IBM, HP3000 and now DEC (oops, sorry
COMPAQ) platforms since 1972 (although I also spent some years in
Systems Analysis, Computer operations techical support and supervisory
posts).

I would like to give my opinion on what I think should be priority
objectives in any new cobol standard.

The strengths of cobol have always been in its ease of use in
commercial data processing, in backroom batch processing, its very
simple English-like non-cryptic commands, its inherent
self-documention (especially if written in a structured manner),
strong portability between many platforms, comparative easier to
understand error messages, clear division into Data Division and
Procedure Division (which in turn is structured into sections,
paragraphs)

It is the above strengths that have persuaded users to continue making
use of the language for the last 30 years despite the many 'newer'
languages that have come and go during the same period.

I feel that in the formulation of any new standard, whether a new
feature is to be added or not should be based on whether it contribues
or enhances to the above strengths, and not on the fact that it is the
flavour of the month. If a new feature, which happens to be the
flavour of the month, contrbutes to the above strengths, then it
shoild be added, otherwise it should not. Only in this way, by
focusing, improving and extending the strengths of COBOL can we ensure
that new users will have the same reasons as the earlier users (of the
last 30 years) to continue making use of the language.
   
===================================================

Boon Lee
Melbourne PC User Group

E-mail : boonlee@melbpc.org.au

===================================================
```

---

```
"Darius Cooper" (Darius_cooper@Bigfoot.com) writes:
>>I'm an A student,

> Its easy.
> 
Shh!
COBOL is very difficult to learn, nearly impossible for someone else to
read, or debug, and if you need JCL ohh boy you're in big truble.
Best leave that sort of coding stuff to consultants.  Mortals may be able
to master HTML, and JAVA but COBOL I wouldn't reccomend a beginner even
open a source file.  Alot of them have been booby trapped and if you're
not an expert they may CRASH the system.  That's why they try and keep the
COBOL code on mainframes, PC's will melt if the code goes bad :)
```

<a id="t-168aa002e1"></a>
## Thread: Stupid Headhunter Tricks - anything else — 3 this month / 5 total

_Topics: [`Jobs, careers, recruiting, salary`](topics.md#jobs)_

### Re: Stupid Headhunter Tricks - anything else

- **From:** Klint Kendrick <csi5@sprintmail.com>
- **Date:** 1998-06-28T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,comp.software.year-2000
- **Message-ID:** `<35968C36.F43AD02D@sprintmail.com>`
- **References:** `<VA.000008f1.000192b9@access.digex.net> <01bd9a07$d883b240$b0e82ac2@default> <7kiYjIAZh9h1EwQ5@elmbronze.demon.co.uk> <6m99l4$i7r$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <z5qKkOA0owi1Ew4T@elmbronze.demon.co.uk>`

```

I've greatly enjoyed reading this thread.  As a neophyte "bloodsucking pimp" I'm
glad to have the eons of experience this group has to offer in the "what not to
do" category.

I've seen a few of my own snafus surface, and appreciate the help dejanews gave
me in finding this highly-amusing thread.  For example, there is such a love/hate
relationship between the contractors, the clients, and the recruiters.  I'm not
sure I've seen one civil word about anybody except the poster (the curse of
usenet perhaps?).  Makes me wonder how most of these posters survive a standard
interview cycle.....

Some insight....

In attempting to achieve a fine balance between contractor happiness (that's how
I get referrals) and client happiness (let's face it, that's how I get paid), I
need to protect both sides. Quite frankly, if you're not working with someone who
is willing to do what needs to be done, you should find a different
agency/headhunter.

I respect the contractors by ensuring that I know the details of the job:  pay
range, skill set, location.  I don't dick around with their time because I read a
resume (if available) before calling.  I try to actually listen.  My company pays
weekly, (but we only do W-2).  If a resume or posting says "No recruiters" that's
fine with me.  I don't call because, hey, it's their loss :)  I also attempt to
ensure that they get the best rate possible.  This is how I get paid.  My
commissions (and this is industry standard) are based on the margins involved
(Typically 50% margin, 20% of which goes to taxes and overhead /i.e. pay rate
=$50, bill rate ($50 x 1.5 = $75), gross margin ($25 x .8 = $20)/  I'm
commissioned off of that $20.  Honestly, I don't see why the $50/hr employee
should complain about that, if it's a fair rate.  This is what protects the
contractor, the more they make, the more I make.

I respect my client by ensuring that I meet face-to-face with any local
contractor I place.  I check at least two references and verify pertinent
information before setting up an interview.  I determine their needs in detail
(and not by talking to a personnel jockey, but by discussing things with the
hiring manager).  I make sure I understand the terminology so I can properly
assess the candidates.  I make sure that the best people get in the door.  And,
yes, they are my bread and butter.  I've never been paid by a
candidate/contractor for a placement/assignment.

Yeah, I occasionally screw up and miss the mark, but at least I try. BTW, this
nonsense about potential litigation against an individual within a company is
pure nonsense.  I'd consult a lawyer before expecting any great result from a
suit against one (usually indemnified) individual.  I suspect the poster was just
pissed ( or perhaps he's one of the liberal arts majors that failed law school).


Klint C. Kendrick

"If pro is the opposite of con, what's the opposite of Congress?"
```

#### ↳ Re: Stupid Headhunter Tricks - anything else

- **From:** The Goobers <docdwarf@erols.com>
- **Date:** 1998-06-28T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,comp.software.year-2000
- **Message-ID:** `<35969E8D.1BF4@erols.com>`
- **References:** `<VA.000008f1.000192b9@access.digex.net> <01bd9a07$d883b240$b0e82ac2@default> <7kiYjIAZh9h1EwQ5@elmbronze.demon.co.uk> <6m99l4$i7r$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <z5qKkOA0owi1Ew4T@elmbronze.demon.co.uk> <35968C36.F43AD02D@sprintmail.com>`

```

Klint Kendrick wrote:
> 
> I've greatly enjoyed reading this thread.  As a neophyte "bloodsucking pimp" I'm
> glad to have the eons of experience this group has to offer in the "what not to
> do" category.

Glad you got something out of it... part of what UseNet's for, sure.

> 
> I've seen a few of my own snafus surface, and appreciate the help dejanews gave
…[4 more quoted lines elided]…
> interview cycle.....

Speaking only for myself, of course, I survive based on intelligence,
intuition and a *ruthless* devotion to the quality of my work. 
Curiously enough what is most frequently held against me and proves to
be my undoing is... intelligence, intuition and a *ruthless* devotion to
the quality of my work.

> 
> Some insight....
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> agency/headhunter.

Whenever it has boiled down to 'will the contractor be happy?' versus
'will the client be happy?' I have never seen it decided towards the
former, rather than the latter... but this is just my experience, of
course.

> 
> I respect the contractors by ensuring that I know the details of the job:  pay
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> contractor, the more they make, the more I make.

WHOOP WOOP WOOP!  The alarm bells go off... this is, in my experience,
out-and-out *wrong*  The more the *client* pays, the more *you* make...
the less you can get the consultant to settle for, the more *you* make. 
The ideal situation would be for you to find a client willing to pay
infinitely high rates and a consultant willing to accept infinitely low
ones... guess who makes more then?

Give us no noble phrases... let us see the invoices you send the client.

> 
> I respect my client by ensuring that I meet face-to-face with any local
> contractor I place.

Respect your client?  You must work for a... different sort of agency;
many agencies I have dealt with grade their pimps on a variety of sorts
of contacts... phone call is one, returned phone call is another, phone
presentation another, phone tech another, 'hairy ears' interview ('does
s/he know how to dress?  is there hair springing forth from the ears?')
yet another.  If you want to nigh *guarantee* a face-to-face with a
consultant then offer to buy lunch.

> I check at least two references and verify pertinent
> information before setting up an interview.  I determine their needs in detail
> (and not by talking to a personnel jockey, but by discussing things with the
> hiring manager).  I make sure I understand the terminology so I can properly
> assess the candidates.

Gosh, that's nice... learn the field before you try and place folks who
deal in it.  Can you spell VSAM?  Sorry, that *was* nasty... but I find
it odd that your expresion of minimal competence (Know Your Field) is
taken as *anything* but 'for granted'.

DD
```

##### ↳ ↳ Re: Stupid Headhunter Tricks - anything else

- **From:** "Donald Tees" <donald@willmack.com>
- **Date:** 1998-06-28T00:00:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol,comp.software.year-2000
- **Message-ID:** `<6n6brk$i0a$1@news.igs.net>`
- **References:** `<VA.000008f1.000192b9@access.digex.net> <01bd9a07$d883b240$b0e82ac2@default> <7kiYjIAZh9h1EwQ5@elmbronze.demon.co.uk> <6m99l4$i7r$1@nnrp1.dejanews.com> <z5qKkOA0owi1Ew4T@elmbronze.demon.co.uk> <35968C36.F43AD02D@sprintmail.com> <35969E8D.1BF4@erols.com>`

```

>WHOOP WOOP WOOP!  The alarm bells go off... this is, in my >experience,
>out-and-out *wrong*  The more the *client* pays, the more *you* make...
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>ones... guess who makes more then?

To tell the truth, in 25 years of freelancing, I have never yet
run into this.  Perhaps it is a local thing (I am in Canada). The
body shops around here all work on a percentage basis.

The norm seems to be either a 70/30 split or a 85/15 split,
depending upon who does the invoicing and financing.
IE- at 70/30, I turn in my timesheets (signed), and get paid.
At 85/15, the customer is billed and I get paid when the money
arrives.  I always considered that reasonable, as the
sales cycle is expensive.  One salesman can make a decent
living by keeping half a dozen programmers working ... a full
time job.
```
